I've uploaded a python code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
[Bug]: Regression in alpha config upstreams with regex (+rewrite target)
### OAuth2-Proxy Version

7.6.0

### Provider

google

### Expected Behaviour

In 7.5.1 we were running the following upstreamConfig

```
      upstreamConfig:
        upstreams:
          - id: app
            path: ^/(.*)$
            rewriteTarget: /$1
            proxyWebSockets: true
            uri: http://app:3000
          - id: api
            path: ^/api(/stripe/webhook|/graphql|/downloads)(.*)$
            rewriteTarget: /api$1$2
            proxyWebSockets: true
            uri: http://api:5555
```

Where all our requests went to the app except a few prefixed by /api/graphql for example.

### Current Behaviour

Upgrading to 7.6.0, this no longer works. All requests to the app end up returning the html served on / (in our example the base html from NextJS, but all js/css/etc also returns that base html) In a similar fashion, all things accessing the api component return the /api endpoint on the /api route.

I've tried with httpbin to see if is was on our side, but also here it can only serve / and not any other routes.

The output in the logs is the same as in 7.5.1

![CleanShot 2024-02-15 at 11 27 44@2x](https://github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/assets/16780/c44778ee-80a5-4737-9e9a-05f66fff091f)

In this screenshot both / and /spec.js return the contents of /

I saw some more logger calls in the go code but i'm unsure on how to get these printed out.

- Changing the container version to 7.5.1 and all works again as it should
- the -alpine container of 7.6.0 has the same issue, so it is not the image itself
- I've scanned all commits that went into 7.6.0 but cannot find any change that is related, my guess is that it might have been one of the dependency updates

### Steps To Reproduce

1. helm install the 7.5.1 version
2. configure the upstreams like above
3. WORKS
4. upgrade the helm chart (image goes to 7.6.0
5. ERROR
6. change just the image version of the deployment to 7.5.1
7. WORKS

### Possible Solutions

_No response_

### Configuration details or additional information

_No response_

</pr_description>

     3	import (

     5	        "net/http"

     8	        "strings"
     9	
    10	        "github.com/justinas/alice"
    11	        "github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/apis/middleware"
    12	        "github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/app/pagewriter"
    13	        "github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/logger"
    14	)
    15	
    16	// newRewritePath creates a new middleware that will rewrite the request URI
    17	// path before handing the request to the next server.
    18	func newRewritePath(rewriteRegExp *regexp.Regexp, rewriteTarget string, writer pagewriter.Writer) alice.Constructor {
    19	        return func(next http.Handler) http.Handler {
    20	                return rewritePath(rewriteRegExp, rewriteTarget, writer, next)
    21	        }
    22	}
    23	
    24	// rewritePath uses the regexp to rewrite the request URI based on the provided
    25	// rewriteTarget.
    26	func rewritePath(rewriteRegExp *regexp.Regexp, rewriteTarget string, writer pagewriter.Writer, next http.Handler) http.Handler {
    27	        return http.HandlerFunc(func(rw http.ResponseWriter, req *http.Request) {
    28	                reqURL, err := url.ParseRequestURI(req.RequestURI)
    29	                if err != nil {
    30	                        logger.Errorf("could not parse request URI: %v", err)
    31	                        writer.WriteErrorPage(rw, pagewriter.ErrorPageOpts{
    32	                                Status:    http.StatusInternalServerError,
    33	                                RequestID: middleware.GetRequestScope(req).RequestID,
    34	                                AppError:  fmt.Sprintf("Could not parse request URI: %v", err),
    35	                        })
    36	                        return
    37	                }
    38	
    39	                // Use the regex to rewrite the request path before proxying to the upstream.
    40	                newURI := rewriteRegExp.ReplaceAllString(reqURL.Path, rewriteTarget)
    41	                reqURL.Path, reqURL.RawQuery, err = splitPathAndQuery(reqURL.Query(), newURI)
    42	                if err != nil {
    43	                        logger.Errorf("could not parse rewrite URI: %v", err)
    44	                        writer.WriteErrorPage(rw, pagewriter.ErrorPageOpts{
    45	                                Status:    http.StatusInternalServerError,
    46	                                RequestID: middleware.GetRequestScope(req).RequestID,
    47	                                AppError:  fmt.Sprintf("Could not parse rewrite URI: %v", err),
    48	                        })
    49	                        return
    50	                }
    51	
    52	                req.RequestURI = reqURL.String()
    53	                req.URL.Path = reqURL.Path // set path for websocket connections
    54	                next.ServeHTTP(rw, req)
    55	        })
    56	}
    57	
    58	// splitPathAndQuery splits the rewritten path into the URL Path and the URL
    59	// raw query. Any rewritten query values are appended to the original query
    60	// values.
    61	// This relies on the underlying URL library to encode the query string.
    62	// For duplicate values it appends each as a separate value, e.g. ?foo=bar&foo=baz.
    63	func splitPathAndQuery(originalQuery url.Values, raw string) (string, string, error) {
    64	        s := strings.SplitN(raw, "?", 2)
    65	        if len(s) == 1 {
    66	                return s[0], originalQuery.Encode(), nil
    67	        }
    68	
    69	        queryValues, err := url.ParseQuery(s[1])
    70	        if err != nil {
    71	                return "", "", nil
    72	        }
    73	
    74	        for key, values := range queryValues {
    75	                for _, value := range values {
    76	                        originalQuery.Add(key, value)
    77	                }
    78	        }
    79	
    80	        return s[0], originalQuery.Encode(), nil
    81	}
    82

     2	
     3	import (
     4	        "context"
     5	        "fmt"
     6	        "net/http"
     7	        "net/url"

     9	        "sort"
    10	        "strings"

    13	        "github.com/justinas/alice"
    14	        "github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/apis/options"
    15	        "github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/app/pagewriter"
    16	        "github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/logger"
    17	)
    18	
    19	// ProxyErrorHandler is a function that will be used to render error pages when
    20	// HTTP proxies fail to connect to upstream servers.
    21	type ProxyErrorHandler func(http.ResponseWriter, *http.Request, error)
    22	
    23	// NewProxy creates a new multiUpstreamProxy that can serve requests directed to
    24	// multiple upstreams.
    25	func NewProxy(upstreams options.UpstreamConfig, sigData *options.SignatureData, writer pagewriter.Writer) (http.Handler, error) {
    26	        m := &multiUpstreamProxy{
    27	                serveMux: mux.NewRouter(),
    28	        }
    29	
    30	        if upstreams.ProxyRawPath {
    31	                m.serveMux.UseEncodedPath()
    32	        }
    33	
    34	        for _, upstream := range sortByPathLongest(upstreams.Upstreams) {
    35	                if upstream.Static {
    36	                        if err := m.registerStaticResponseHandler(upstream, writer); err != nil {
    37	                                return nil, fmt.Errorf("could not register static upstream %q: %v", upstream.ID, err)
    38	                        }
    39	                        continue
    40	                }
    41	
    42	                u, err := url.Parse(upstream.URI)
    43	                if err != nil {
    44	                        return nil, fmt.Errorf("error parsing URI for upstream %q: %w", upstream.ID, err)
    45	                }
    46	                switch u.Scheme {
    47	                case fileScheme:
    48	                        if err := m.registerFileServer(upstream, u, writer); err != nil {
    49	                                return nil, fmt.Errorf("could not register file upstream %q: %v", upstream.ID, err)
    50	                        }
    51	                case httpScheme, httpsScheme, unixScheme:
    52	                        if err := m.registerHTTPUpstreamProxy(upstream, u, sigData, writer); err != nil {
    53	                                return nil, fmt.Errorf("could not register %s upstream %q: %v", u.Scheme, upstream.ID, err)
    54	                        }
    55	                default:
    56	                        return nil, fmt.Errorf("unknown scheme for upstream %q: %q", upstream.ID, u.Scheme)
    57	                }
    58	        }
    59	
    60	        registerTrailingSlashHandler(m.serveMux)
    61	        return m, nil
    62	}
    63	
    64	// multiUpstreamProxy will serve requests directed to multiple upstream servers
    65	// registered in the serverMux.
    66	type multiUpstreamProxy struct {
    67	        serveMux *mux.Router
    68	}
    69	
    70	// ServerHTTP handles HTTP requests.
    71	func (m *multiUpstreamProxy) ServeHTTP(rw http.ResponseWriter, req *http.Request) {
    72	        m.serveMux.ServeHTTP(rw, req)
    73	}
    74	
    75	// registerStaticResponseHandler registers a static response handler with at the given path.
    76	func (m *multiUpstreamProxy) registerStaticResponseHandler(upstream options.Upstream, writer pagewriter.Writer) error {
    77	        logger.Printf("mapping path %q => static response %d", upstream.Path, derefStaticCode(upstream.StaticCode))
    78	        return m.registerHandler(upstream, newStaticResponseHandler(upstream.ID, upstream.StaticCode), writer)
    79	}
    80	
    81	// registerFileServer registers a new fileServer based on the configuration given.
    82	func (m *multiUpstreamProxy) registerFileServer(upstream options.Upstream, u *url.URL, writer pagewriter.Writer) error {
    83	        logger.Printf("mapping path %q => file system %q", upstream.Path, u.Path)
    84	        return m.registerHandler(upstream, newFileServer(upstream, u.Path), writer)
    85	}
    86	
    87	// registerHTTPUpstreamProxy registers a new httpUpstreamProxy based on the configuration given.
    88	func (m *multiUpstreamProxy) registerHTTPUpstreamProxy(upstream options.Upstream, u *url.URL, sigData *options.SignatureData, writer pagewriter.Writer) error {
    89	        logger.Printf("mapping path %q => upstream %q", upstream.Path, upstream.URI)
    90	        return m.registerHandler(upstream, newHTTPUpstreamProxy(upstream, u, sigData, writer.ProxyErrorHandler), writer)
    91	}
    92	
    93	// registerHandler ensures the given handler is regiestered with the serveMux.
    94	func (m *multiUpstreamProxy) registerHandler(upstream options.Upstream, handler http.Handler, writer pagewriter.Writer) error {
    95	        if upstream.RewriteTarget == "" {
    96	                m.registerSimpleHandler(upstream.Path, handler)
    97	                return nil
    98	        }
    99	
   100	        return m.registerRewriteHandler(upstream, handler, writer)
   101	}
   102	
   103	// registerSimpleHandler maintains the behaviour of the go standard serveMux
   104	// by ensuring any path with a trailing `/` matches all paths under that prefix.
   105	func (m *multiUpstreamProxy) registerSimpleHandler(path string, handler http.Handler) {
   106	        if strings.HasSuffix(path, "/") {
   107	                m.serveMux.PathPrefix(path).Handler(handler)
   108	        } else {
   109	                m.serveMux.Path(path).Handler(handler)
   110	        }
   111	}
   112	
   113	// registerRewriteHandler ensures the handler is registered for all paths
   114	// which match the regex defined in the Path.
   115	// Requests to the handler will have the request path rewritten before the
   116	// request is made to the next handler.
   117	func (m *multiUpstreamProxy) registerRewriteHandler(upstream options.Upstream, handler http.Handler, writer pagewriter.Writer) error {
   118	        rewriteRegExp, err := regexp.Compile(upstream.Path)
   119	        if err != nil {
   120	                return fmt.Errorf("invalid path %q for upstream: %v", upstream.Path, err)
   121	        }
   122	
   123	        rewrite := newRewritePath(rewriteRegExp, upstream.RewriteTarget, writer)
   124	        h := alice.New(rewrite).Then(handler)
   125	        m.serveMux.MatcherFunc(func(req *http.Request, _ *mux.RouteMatch) bool {
   126	                return rewriteRegExp.MatchString(req.URL.Path)
   127	        }).Handler(h)
   128	
   129	        return nil
   130	}
   131	
   132	// registerTrailingSlashHandler creates a new matcher that will check if the
   133	// requested path would match if it had a trailing slash appended.
   134	// If the path matches with a trailing slash, we send back a redirect.
   135	// This allows us to be consistent with the built in go servemux implementation.
   136	func registerTrailingSlashHandler(serveMux *mux.Router) {
   137	        serveMux.MatcherFunc(func(req *http.Request, _ *mux.RouteMatch) bool {
   138	                if strings.HasSuffix(req.URL.Path, "/") {
   139	                        return false
   140	                }
   141	
   142	                // Use a separate RouteMatch so that we can redirect to the path + /.
   143	                // If we pass through the match then the matched backed will be served
   144	                // instead of the redirect handler.
   145	                m := &mux.RouteMatch{}
   146	                slashReq := req.Clone(context.Background())
   147	                slashReq.URL.Path += "/"
   148	                return serveMux.Match(slashReq, m)
   149	        }).Handler(http.HandlerFunc(func(rw http.ResponseWriter, req *http.Request) {
   150	                http.Redirect(rw, req, req.URL.String()+"/", http.StatusMovedPermanently)
   151	        }))
   152	}
   153	
   154	// sortByPathLongest ensures that the upstreams are sorted by longest path.
   155	// If rewrites are involved, a rewrite takes precedence over a non-rewrite.
   156	// When two upstreams define rewrites, whichever has the longest path will take
   157	// precedence (note this is the input to the rewrite logic).
   158	// This does not account for when a rewrite would actually make the path shorter.
   159	// This should maintain the sorting behaviour of the standard go serve mux.
   160	func sortByPathLongest(in []options.Upstream) []options.Upstream {
   161	        sort.Slice(in, func(i, j int) bool {
   162	                iRW := in[i].RewriteTarget
   163	                jRW := in[j].RewriteTarget
   164	
   165	                switch {
   166	                case iRW != "" && jRW != "":
   167	                        // If both have a rewrite target, whichever has the longest pattern
   168	                        // should go first
   169	                        return len(in[i].Path) > len(in[j].Path)
   170	                case iRW != "" && jRW == "":
   171	                        // Only one has rewrite, it goes first
   172	                        return true
   173	                case iRW == "" && jRW != "":
   174	                        // Only one has rewrite, it goes first
   175	                        return false
   176	                default:
   177	                        // Default to longest Path wins
   178	                        return len(in[i].Path) > len(in[j].Path)
   179	                }
   180	        })
   181	        return in
   182	}
   183

commit 7529095e1ac4304d373a5f9774f8dea2d6bd9435
Author: Marius Zander <marius@bam-bam-bam.com>
Date:   Wed Jun 14 17:49:08 2023 +0200

    fix: use X-Forwarded-Uri if it exists for pathRegex match
    
    the functions `isApiPath` and `isAllowedPath` use the `req.URL.Path` property which leads to faulty behavior when behind a reverse proxy. The correct path can be inferred from the `X-Forwarded-Uri` header by making use of the already provided `requestutil.GetRequestURI` function.
    
    Co-authored-by: Jan Wystub <jan@bam-bam-bam.com>

diff --git a/oauthproxy.go b/oauthproxy.go
index 7398fb8e..25b14e61 100644
--- a/oauthproxy.go
+++ b/oauthproxy.go
@@ -554,7 +554,7 @@ func isAllowedMethod(req *http.Request, route allowedRoute) bool {
 }
 
 func isAllowedPath(req *http.Request, route allowedRoute) bool {
-	matches := route.pathRegex.MatchString(req.URL.Path)
+	matches := route.pathRegex.MatchString(requestutil.GetRequestURI(req))
 
 	if route.negate {
 		return !matches
@@ -575,7 +575,7 @@ func (p *OAuthProxy) isAllowedRoute(req *http.Request) bool {
 
 func (p *OAuthProxy) isAPIPath(req *http.Request) bool {
 	for _, route := range p.apiRoutes {
-		if route.pathRegex.MatchString(req.URL.Path) {
+		if route.pathRegex.MatchString(requestutil.GetRequestURI(req)) {
 			return true
 		}
 	}

+// Unix implementation of http.RoundTripper, required to register unix protocol in reverse proxy
+type unixRoundTripper struct {
+	Transport *http.Transport
+}
+
+// Implementation of https://pkg.go.dev/net/http#RoundTripper interface to support http protocol over unix socket
+func (t *unixRoundTripper) RoundTrip(req *http.Request) (*http.Response, error) {
+	// Inspired by https://github.com/tv42/httpunix
+	// Not having a Host, even if not used, makes the reverseproxy fail with a "no Host in request URL"
+	if req.Host == "" {
+		req.Host = "localhost"
+	}
+	req.URL.Host = req.Host
+	tt := t.Transport
+	req = req.Clone(req.Context())
+	req.URL.Scheme = "http"
+	return tt.RoundTrip(req)
+}
+
 // newReverseProxy creates a new reverse proxy for proxying requests to upstream
 // servers based on the upstream configuration provided.
 // The proxy should render an error page if there are failures connecting to the
@@ -102,6 +127,14 @@ func newReverseProxy(target *url.URL, upstream options.Upstream, errorHandler Pr
 	// Inherit default transport options from Go's stdlib
 	transport := http.DefaultTransport.(*http.Transport).Clone()
 
+	if target.Scheme == "unix" {
+		transport.DialContext = func(ctx context.Context, _, _ string) (net.Conn, error) {
+			dialer := net.Dialer{}
+			return dialer.DialContext(ctx, target.Scheme, target.Path)
+		}
+		transport.RegisterProtocol(target.Scheme, &unixRoundTripper{Transport: transport})
+	}
+
 	// Change default duration for waiting for an upstream response
 	if upstream.Timeout != nil {
 		transport.ResponseHeaderTimeout = upstream.Timeout.Duration()

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_regex_upstream.go --file_text 'package main

import (
	"encoding/json"
	"fmt"
	"net/http"
	"net/http/httptest"

	"github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/apis/options"
	"github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/app/pagewriter"
	"github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/upstream"
)

type TestResponse struct {
	Path string `json:"path"`
}

func main() {
	// Create a test HTTP server that echoes back the request path
	testServer := httptest.NewServer(http.HandlerFunc(func(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {
		response := TestResponse{Path: r.URL.Path}
		json.NewEncoder(w).Encode(response)
	}))
	defer testServer.Close()

	// Create upstream configuration like in the bug report
	upstreamConfig := options.UpstreamConfig{
		Upstreams: []options.Upstream{
			{
				ID:            "app",
				Path:          "^/(.*)$",
				RewriteTarget: "/$1",
				URI:           testServer.URL,
			},
		},
	}

	sigData := &options.SignatureData{}
	writer := &pagewriter.WriterFuncs{}

	proxy, err := upstream.NewProxy(upstreamConfig, sigData, writer)
	if err != nil {
		fmt.Printf("Error creating proxy: %v\n", err)
		return
	}

	// Test various paths
	testPaths := []string{
		"/",
		"/spec.js",
		"/api/test",
		"/foo/bar",
	}

	for _, path := range testPaths {
		req := httptest.NewRequest("GET", "http://localhost"+path, nil)
		rw := httptest.NewRecorder()
		
		proxy.ServeHTTP(rw, req)
		
		fmt.Printf("Request: %s => Status: %d, Body: %s\n", path, rw.Code, rw.Body.String())
	}
}
'

	Path string `json:"path"`
}

func main() {
	// Create a test HTTP server that echoes back the request path

import (
	"crypto"
	"encoding/json"
	"fmt"
	"net/http"
	"net/http/httptest"

	"github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/apis/options"
	"github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/app/pagewriter"
	"github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/upstream"
)

type TestResponse struct {
	Path string `json:"path"`
}

func main() {
	// Create a test HTTP server that echoes back the request path
	testServer := httptest.NewServer(http.HandlerFunc(func(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {
		response := TestResponse{Path: r.URL.Path}
		json.NewEncoder(w).Encode(response)
	}))
	defer testServer.Close()

	// Create upstream configuration like in the bug report
	upstreamConfig := options.UpstreamConfig{
		Upstreams: []options.Upstream{
			{
				ID:            "app",
				Path:          "^/(.*)$",
				RewriteTarget: "/$1",
				URI:           testServer.URL,
			},
		},
	}

		Key:  "secret",
	}
	writer := &pagewriter.WriterFuncs{}'

   114	// which match the regex defined in the Path.
   115	// Requests to the handler will have the request path rewritten before the
   116	// request is made to the next handler.
   117	func (m *multiUpstreamProxy) registerRewriteHandler(upstream options.Upstream, handler http.Handler, writer pagewriter.Writer) error {
   118	        rewriteRegExp, err := regexp.Compile(upstream.Path)
   119	        if err != nil {
   120	                return fmt.Errorf("invalid path %q for upstream: %v", upstream.Path, err)

commit 395ad81d0ebffa0c5a36f3e5a2e720a7d5870d92
Author: Soheil Rahmat <soheilrt314@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Aug 17 04:34:43 2023 +0300

    [BUG] Inconsistent HTTP status code on query mismatch (#712)
    
    The logical behavior of a router should return an HTTP status code of
    404 when a request fails to satisfy route validation logic. Previously,
    MUX was returning a 405 HTTP status code in some rare scenarios, which
    was not valid in its case.
    
    For more info, See: https://github.com/gorilla/mux/issues/704
    
    Fixes #704
    
    **Summary of Changes**
    
    1. Clear the mismatch error of the previous validations on method match.
    2. Added related tests
    
    > PS: Make sure your PR includes/updates tests! If you need help with
    this part, just ask!
    
    Co-authored-by: Corey Daley <cdaley@redhat.com>

+func TestMultipleDefinitionOfSamePathWithDifferentMethods(t *testing.T) {
+	emptyHandler := func(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {}
+
+	r := NewRouter()
+	r.HandleFunc("/api", emptyHandler).Methods("POST")
+	r.HandleFunc("/api", emptyHandler).Queries("time", "{time:[0-9]+}").Methods("GET")
+
+	t.Run("Post Method should be matched properly", func(t *testing.T) {
+		req, _ := http.NewRequest("POST", "http://localhost/api", nil)
+		match := new(RouteMatch)
+		matched := r.Match(req, match)
+		if !matched {
+			t.Error("Should have matched route for methods")
+		}
+		if match.MatchErr != nil {
+			t.Error("Should not have any matching error. Found:", match.MatchErr)
+		}
+	})
+
+	t.Run("Get Method with invalid query value should not match", func(t *testing.T) {
+		req, _ := http.NewRequest("GET", "http://localhost/api?time=-4", nil)
+		match := new(RouteMatch)
+		matched := r.Match(req, match)
+		if matched {
+			t.Error("Should not have matched route for methods")
+		}
+		if match.MatchErr != ErrNotFound {
+			t.Error("Should have ErrNotFound error. Found:", match.MatchErr)
+		}
+	})
+
+	t.Run("A mismach method of a valid path should return ErrMethodMismatch", func(t *testing.T) {
+		r := NewRouter()
+		r.HandleFunc("/api2", emptyHandler).Methods("POST")
+		req, _ := http.NewRequest("GET", "http://localhost/api2", nil)
+		match := new(RouteMatch)
+		matched := r.Match(req, match)
+		if matched {
+			t.Error("Should not have matched route for methods")
+		}
+		if match.MatchErr != ErrMethodMismatch {
+			t.Error("Should have ErrMethodMismatch error. Found:", match.MatchErr)
+		}
+	})
+
+}

    74	type httpUpstreamProxy struct {
    75	        upstream  string
    76	        handler   http.Handler
    77	        wsHandler http.Handler
    78	        auth      hmacauth.HmacAuth

    81	// ServeHTTP proxies requests to the upstream provider while signing the
    82	// request headers
    83	func (h *httpUpstreamProxy) ServeHTTP(rw http.ResponseWriter, req *http.Request) {
    84	        scope := middleware.GetRequestScope(req)
    85	        // If scope is nil, this will panic.
    86	        // A scope should always be injected before this handler is called.
    87	        scope.Upstream = h.upstream
    88

    94	        if h.wsHandler != nil && strings.EqualFold(req.Header.Get("Connection"), "upgrade") && req.Header.Get("Upgrade") == "websocket" {

    96	        } else {

   100	
   101	// Unix implementation of http.RoundTripper, required to register unix protocol in reverse proxy
   102	type unixRoundTripper struct {
   103	        Transport *http.Transport
   104	}
   105	
   106	// Implementation of https://pkg.go.dev/net/http#RoundTripper interface to support http protocol over unix socket
   107	func (t *unixRoundTripper) RoundTrip(req *http.Request) (*http.Response, error) {
   108	        // Inspired by https://github.com/tv42/httpunix
   109	        // Not having a Host, even if not used, makes the reverseproxy fail with a "no Host in request URL"
   110	        if req.Host == "" {
   111	                req.Host = "localhost"
   112	        }
   113	        req.URL.Host = req.Host
   114	        tt := t.Transport
   115	        req = req.Clone(req.Context())
   116	        req.URL.Scheme = "http"
   117	        return tt.RoundTrip(req)
   118	}
   119	
   120	// newReverseProxy creates a new reverse proxy for proxying requests to upstream
   121	// servers based on the upstream configuration provided.
   122	// The proxy should render an error page if there are failures connecting to the
   123	// upstream server.
   124	func newReverseProxy(target *url.URL, upstream options.Upstream, errorHandler ProxyErrorHandler) http.Handler {
   125	        proxy := httputil.NewSingleHostReverseProxy(target)
   126	
   127	        // Inherit default transport options from Go's stdlib
   128	        transport := http.DefaultTransport.(*http.Transport).Clone()
   129	
   130	        if target.Scheme == "unix" {
   131	                transport.DialContext = func(ctx context.Context, _, _ string) (net.Conn, error) {
   132	                        dialer := net.Dialer{}
   133	                        return dialer.DialContext(ctx, target.Scheme, target.Path)
   134	                }
   135	                transport.RegisterProtocol(target.Scheme, &unixRoundTripper{Transport: transport})
   136	        }
   137	
   138	        // Change default duration for waiting for an upstream response
   139	        if upstream.Timeout != nil {
   140	                transport.ResponseHeaderTimeout = upstream.Timeout.Duration()
   141	        }
   142	
   143	        // Configure options on the SingleHostReverseProxy
   144	        if upstream.FlushInterval != nil {
   145	                proxy.FlushInterval = upstream.FlushInterval.Duration()
   146	        } else {
   147	                proxy.FlushInterval = options.DefaultUpstreamFlushInterval
   148	        }
   149	
   150	        // InsecureSkipVerify is a configurable option we allow

# V7.6.0

## Release Highlights

## Important Notes

## Breaking Changes

## Changes since v7.5.1

- [#2381](https://github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/pull/2381) Allow username authentication to Redis cluster (@rossigee)
--

## Breaking Changes
The following PR introduces a change to how auth routes are evaluated using the flags `skip-auth-route`/`skip-auth-regex`. The new behaviour uses the regex you specify to evaluate the full path including query parameters. For more details please read the detailed description [#2271](https://github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/issues/2271)
- [#2192](https://github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/pull/2192) Use X-Forwarded-Uri if it exists for pathRegex match (@mzndr / @jawys)

## Changes since v7.4.0
- [#2028](https://github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/pull/2028) Update golang.org/x/net to v0.7.0 ato address GHSA-vvpx-j8f3-3w6h (@amrmahdi)
- [#1873](https://github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/pull/1873) Fix empty users with some OIDC providers (@babs)
- [#1882](https://github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/pull/1882) Make `htpasswd.GetUsers` racecondition safe (@babs)
- [#1883](https://github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/pull/1883) Ensure v8 manifest variant is set on docker images (@braunsonm)
- [#1906](https://github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/pull/1906) Fix PKCE code verifier generation to never use UTF-8 characters (@braunsonm)
- [#1839](https://github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/pull/1839) Add readiness checks for deeper health checks (@kobim)
- [#1927](https://github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/pull/1927) Fix default scope settings for none oidc providers (@tuunit)

- `/spec.js` → captures `spec.js` → should rewrite to `/spec.js` ✓
- `/api/graphql` → captures `api/graphql` → should rewrite to `/api/graphql` ✓

But if the second config is `^/api(/stripe/webhook|/graphql|/downloads)(.*)$` with rewrite target `/api$1$2`:
- `/api/graphql` → captures `/graphql` in $1, `` in $2 → should rewrite to `/api/graphql` ✓

So the regex should work. Unless... wait! Let me check if maybe the regex isn't matching at all, and there's a fallback that's causing the issue!

Let me look at the routing order in proxy.go more carefully. Looking at line 125-127:

```go
m.serveMux.MatcherFunc(func(req *http.Request, _ *mux.RouteMatch) bool {
    return rewriteRegExp.MatchString(req.URL.Path)
}).Handler(h)
```

This registers a matcher with gorilla/mux. But I notice that there's no priority or anything. And the `sortByPathLongest` function (line 154-181) is supposed to ensure proper ordering.

Oh wait! I think I found it! Look at the `sortByPathLongest` function. It sorts by path length for rewrites. But when the path is a regex like `^/(.*)$`, the length is 8 characters. And `^/api(/stripe/webhook|/graphql|/downloads)(.*)$` is much longer.

So if we register them in order as they appear in the config:
1. First `^/(.*)$` with length 8
2. Second `^/api(/stripe/webhook|/graphql|/downloads)(.*)$` with length much longer

After sorting by `sortByPathLongest`, the second one (longer) will be tried first. This is correct.

But wait, gorilla/mux processes routes in the order they're registered! And the sort happens BEFORE registration. So the longer regex upstream SHOULD be registered first and thus tried first by mux.

Let me double-check the sort logic:

```go
sort.Slice(in, func(i, j int) bool {
    iRW := in[i].RewriteTarget
    jRW := in[j].RewriteTarget

    switch {
    case iRW != "" && jRW != "":
        // If both have a rewrite target, whichever has the longest pattern
        // should go first
        return len(in[i].Path) > len(in[j].Path)
    ...
```

So if both have rewrite targets, longest path wins. That's correct.

But wait! The problem might be that gorilla/mux, starting from v1.8.1, might be handling MatcherFunc routes differently!

Let me check the mux code to see how MatcherFunc routes are matched:

func (r *Route) Match(req *http.Request, match *RouteMatch) bool {
	if r.buildOnly || r.err != nil {
		return false
	}

	var matchErr error

	// Match everything.
	for _, m := range r.matchers {
		if matched := m.Match(req, match); !matched {
			if _, ok := m.(methodMatcher); ok {
				matchErr = ErrMethodMismatch
				continue
			}

			// Ignore ErrNotFound errors. These errors arise from match call
			// to Subrouters.
			//
			// This prevents subsequent matching subrouters from failing to
			// run middleware. If not ignored, the middleware would see a
			// non-nil MatchErr and be skipped, even when there was a
			// matching route.
			if match.MatchErr == ErrNotFound {
				match.MatchErr = nil
			}

			matchErr = nil
			return false
		}
	}

	if matchErr != nil {
		match.MatchErr = matchErr
		return false
	}

	if match.MatchErr == ErrMethodMismatch && r.handler != nil {
		// We found a route which matches request method, clear MatchErr
		match.MatchErr = nil
		// Then override the mis-matched handler
		match.Handler = r.handler
--
func (r *Route) MatcherFunc(f MatcherFunc) *Route {
	return r.addMatcher(f)
}

// Methods --------------------------------------------------------------------

// methodMatcher matches the request against HTTP methods.
type methodMatcher []string

func (m methodMatcher) Match(r *http.Request, match *RouteMatch) bool {
	return matchInArray(m, r.Method)
}

// Methods adds a matcher for HTTP methods.
// It accepts a sequence of one or more methods to be matched, e.g.:
// "GET", "POST", "PUT".
func (r *Route) Methods(methods ...string) *Route {
	for k, v := range methods {
		methods[k] = strings.ToUpper(v)
	}
	return r.addMatcher(methodMatcher(methods))
}

// - {name:pattern} matches the given regexp pattern.

// For example:
//
//     r := mux.NewRouter()
//     r.Path("/products/").Handler(ProductsHandler)
//     r.Path("/products/{key}").Handler(ProductsHandler)
//     r.Path("/articles/{category}/{id:[0-9]+}").
//       Handler(ArticleHandler)

func (r *Route) Match(req *http.Request, match *RouteMatch) bool {
	if r.buildOnly || r.err != nil {
		return false
	}

	var matchErr error

	// Match everything.
	for _, m := range r.matchers {
		if matched := m.Match(req, match); !matched {
			if _, ok := m.(methodMatcher); ok {
				matchErr = ErrMethodMismatch
				continue
			}

			// Ignore ErrNotFound errors. These errors arise from match call
			// to Subrouters.
			//
			// This prevents subsequent matching subrouters from failing to
			// run middleware. If not ignored, the middleware would see a
			// non-nil MatchErr and be skipped, even when there was a
			// matching route.
			if match.MatchErr == ErrNotFound {
				match.MatchErr = nil
			}

			matchErr = nil // nolint:ineffassign
			return false
		} else {
			// Multiple routes may share the same path but use different HTTP methods. For instance:
			// Route 1: POST "/users/{id}".
			// Route 2: GET "/users/{id}", parameters: "id": "[0-9]+".
			//
			// The router must handle these cases correctly. For a GET request to "/users/abc" with "id" as "-2",
			// The router should return a "Not Found" error as no route fully matches this request.
			if match.MatchErr == ErrMethodMismatch {
				match.MatchErr = nil
			}
		}
	}

	if matchErr != nil {
		match.MatchErr = matchErr
		return false
	}

	if match.MatchErr == ErrMethodMismatch && r.handler != nil {
		// We found a route which matches request method, clear MatchErr
		match.MatchErr = nil
		// Then override the mis-matched handler
		match.Handler = r.handler
--
func (r *Route) MatcherFunc(f MatcherFunc) *Route {
	return r.addMatcher(f)
}

// methodMatcher matches the request against HTTP methods.
type methodMatcher []string

func (m methodMatcher) Match(r *http.Request, match *RouteMatch) bool {
	return matchInArray(m, r.Method)
}

// Methods adds a matcher for HTTP methods.
// It accepts a sequence of one or more methods to be matched, e.g.:
// "GET", "POST", "PUT".
func (r *Route) Methods(methods ...string) *Route {
	for k, v := range methods {
		methods[k] = strings.ToUpper(v)
	}
	return r.addMatcher(methodMatcher(methods))
}

// Path -----------------------------------------------------------------------

// Path adds a matcher for the URL path.
// It accepts a template with zero or more URL variables enclosed by {}. The
// template must start with a "/".
// Variables can define an optional regexp pattern to be matched:
//
// - {name} matches anything until the next slash.
//
// - {name:pattern} matches the given regexp pattern.
//
// For example:
//
//	r := mux.NewRouter().NewRoute()
//	r.Path("/products/").Handler(ProductsHandler)
//	r.Path("/products/{key}").Handler(ProductsHandler)
//	r.Path("/articles/{category}/{id:[0-9]+}").
//	  Handler(ArticleHandler)
//
// Variable names must be unique in a given route. They can be retrieved
// calling mux.Vars(request).
func (r *Route) Path(tpl string) *Route {
	r.err = r.addRegexpMatcher(tpl, regexpTypePath)
	return r
}

package main

import (
	"fmt"
	"regexp"
)

func main() {
	// Test the regex from the bug report
	rewriteRegExp := regexp.MustCompile("^/(.*)$")
	rewriteTarget := "/$1"
	
	testPaths := []string{
		"/",
		"/spec.js",
		"/api/test",
		"/foo/bar",
	}
	
	for _, path := range testPaths {
		newURI := rewriteRegExp.ReplaceAllString(path, rewriteTarget)
		fmt.Printf("Path: %s => Rewritten: %s\n", path, newURI)
	}
}
EOF

+func TestMultipleDefinitionOfSamePathWithDifferentQueries(t *testing.T) {
+	emptyHandler := func(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {}
+
+	r := NewRouter()
+	r.HandleFunc("/api", emptyHandler).Queries("foo", "{foo:[0-9]+}").Methods(http.MethodGet)
+	r.HandleFunc("/api", emptyHandler).Queries("bar", "{bar:[0-9]+}").Methods(http.MethodGet)
+
+	req := newRequest(http.MethodGet, "/api?bar=4")
+	match := new(RouteMatch)
+	matched := r.Match(req, match)
+	if !matched {
+		t.Error("Should have matched route for methods")
+	}
+	if match.MatchErr != nil {
+		t.Error("Should have no error. Found:", match.MatchErr)
+	}
+}

The tests show that requests to `/rewrite-prefix/1234/abc` should be rewritten to `/different/backend/path/1234/abc`. And the tests pass. So the basic functionality works.

Let me think about what could be different in the user's environment. They're behind an ingress controller... maybe there's something with  X-Forwarded headers? But we already established that X-Forwarded-Uri changes were only for auth routes, not upstream routes.

Wait! Let me check if maybe the ReverseProxy itself is resetting req.URL before the rewrite middleware runs! Let me look at the handler chain:

In `registerRewriteHandler`:
```go
rewrite := newRewritePath(rewriteRegExp, upstream.RewriteTarget, writer)
h := alice.New(rewrite).Then(handler)
```

So the order is: rewrite middleware → handler (which is the httpUpstreamProxy)

And in httpUpstreamProxy.ServeHTTP:
```go
h.handler.ServeHTTP(rw, req)
```

Where `h.handler` is the reverse proxy. So the rewrite happens BEFORE the reverse proxy. That's correct.

OK, I'm going to try a different strategy. Let me look for any related issues in the oauth2-proxy github issues:

# V7.7.0

  - CVE-2024-24791

  - CVE-2024-24784

- Remove support of arm/v6 for distroless image runtime. Alpine tags still support arm/v6.

diff --git a/docs/docs/configuration/alpha_config.md b/docs/docs/configuration/alpha_config.md
index 5bbf891d..fc7c384a 100644
--- a/docs/docs/configuration/alpha_config.md
+++ b/docs/docs/configuration/alpha_config.md
@@ -524,7 +524,7 @@ Requests will be proxied to this upstream if the path matches the request path.
 | ----- | ---- | ----------- |
 | `id` | _string_ | ID should be a unique identifier for the upstream.<br/>This value is required for all upstreams. |
 | `path` | _string_ | Path is used to map requests to the upstream server.<br/>The closest match will take precedence and all Paths must be unique.<br/>Path can also take a pattern when used with RewriteTarget.<br/>Path segments can be captured and matched using regular experessions.<br/>Eg:<br/>- `^/foo$`: Match only the explicit path `/foo`<br/>- `^/bar/$`: Match any path prefixed with `/bar/`<br/>- `^/baz/(.*)$`: Match any path prefixed with `/baz` and capture the remaining path for use with RewriteTarget |
-| `rewriteTarget` | _string_ | RewriteTarget allows users to rewrite the request path before it is sent to<br/>the upstream server.<br/>Use the Path to capture segments for reuse within the rewrite target.<br/>Eg: With a Path of `^/baz/(.*)`, a RewriteTarget of `/foo/$1` would rewrite<br/>the request `/baz/abc/123` to `/foo/abc/123` before proxying to the<br/>upstream server. |
+| `rewriteTarget` | _string_ | RewriteTarget allows users to rewrite the request path before it is sent to<br/>the upstream server (for an HTTP/HTTPS upstream) or mapped to the filesystem<br/>(for a `file:` upstream).<br/>Use the Path to capture segments for reuse within the rewrite target.<br/>Eg: With a Path of `^/baz/(.*)`, a RewriteTarget of `/foo/$1` would rewrite<br/>the request `/baz/abc/123` to `/foo/abc/123` before proxying to the<br/>upstream server.  Or if the upstream were `file:///app`, a request for<br/>`/baz/info.html` would return the contents of the file `/app/foo/info.html`. |
 | `uri` | _string_ | The URI of the upstream server. This may be an HTTP(S) server of a File<br/>based URL. It may include a path, in which case all requests will be served<br/>under that path.<br/>Eg:<br/>- http://localhost:8080<br/>- https://service.localhost<br/>- https://service.localhost/path<br/>- file://host/path<br/>If the URI's path is "/base" and the incoming request was for "/dir",<br/>the upstream request will be for "/base/dir". |
 | `insecureSkipTLSVerify` | _bool_ | InsecureSkipTLSVerify will skip TLS verification of upstream HTTPS hosts.<br/>This option is insecure and will allow potential Man-In-The-Middle attacks<br/>between OAuth2 Proxy and the upstream server.<br/>Defaults to false. |
 | `static` | _bool_ | Static will make all requests to this upstream have a static response.<br/>The response will have a body of "Authenticated" and a response code<br/>matching StaticCode.<br/>If StaticCode is not set, the response will return a 200 response. |

package upstream

import (
	"fmt"
	"net/http"
	"net/url"
	"regexp"
	"strings"

	"github.com/justinas/alice"
	"github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/apis/middleware"
	"github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/app/pagewriter"
	"github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/logger"
)

// newRewritePath creates a new middleware that will rewrite the request URI
// path before handing the request to the next server.
func newRewritePath(rewriteRegExp *regexp.Regexp, rewriteTarget string, writer pagewriter.Writer) alice.Constructor {
	return func(next http.Handler) http.Handler {
		return rewritePath(rewriteRegExp, rewriteTarget, writer, next)
	}
}

// rewritePath uses the regexp to rewrite the request URI based on the provided
// rewriteTarget.
func rewritePath(rewriteRegExp *regexp.Regexp, rewriteTarget string, writer pagewriter.Writer, next http.Handler) http.Handler {
	return http.HandlerFunc(func(rw http.ResponseWriter, req *http.Request) {
		reqURL, err := url.ParseRequestURI(req.RequestURI)
		if err != nil {
			logger.Errorf("could not parse request URI: %v", err)
			writer.WriteErrorPage(rw, pagewriter.ErrorPageOpts{
				Status:    http.StatusInternalServerError,
				RequestID: middleware.GetRequestScope(req).RequestID,
				AppError:  fmt.Sprintf("Could not parse request URI: %v", err),
			})
			return
		}

		// Use the regex to rewrite the request path before proxying to the upstream.
		newURI := rewriteRegExp.ReplaceAllString(reqURL.Path, rewriteTarget)
		reqURL.Path, reqURL.RawQuery, err = splitPathAndQuery(reqURL.Query(), newURI)
		if err != nil {
			logger.Errorf("could not parse rewrite URI: %v", err)
			writer.WriteErrorPage(rw, pagewriter.ErrorPageOpts{
				Status:    http.StatusInternalServerError,
				RequestID: middleware.GetRequestScope(req).RequestID,
				AppError:  fmt.Sprintf("Could not parse rewrite URI: %v", err),
			})
			return
		}

		req.RequestURI = reqURL.String()
		next.ServeHTTP(rw, req)
	})
}

// splitPathAndQuery splits the rewritten path into the URL Path and the URL
// raw query. Any rewritten query values are appended to the original query
// values.
// This relies on the underlying URL library to encode the query string.
// For duplicate values it appends each as a separate value, e.g. ?foo=bar&foo=baz.
func splitPathAndQuery(originalQuery url.Values, raw string) (string, string, error) {
	s := strings.SplitN(raw, "?", 2)
	if len(s) == 1 {
		return s[0], originalQuery.Encode(), nil
	}

	queryValues, err := url.ParseQuery(s[1])
	if err != nil {
		return "", "", nil
	}

	for key, values := range queryValues {
		for _, value := range values {
			originalQuery.Add(key, value)
		}
	}

	return s[0], originalQuery.Encode(), nil
}

	"fmt"

	"github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/logger"
)

// newRewritePath creates a new middleware that will rewrite the request URI
// path before handing the request to the next server.
func newRewritePath(rewriteRegExp *regexp.Regexp, rewriteTarget string, writer pagewriter.Writer) alice.Constructor {
	return func(next http.Handler) http.Handler {
		return rewritePath(rewriteRegExp, rewriteTarget, writer, next)
	}
}

// rewritePath uses the regexp to rewrite the request URI based on the provided
// rewriteTarget.
func rewritePath(rewriteRegExp *regexp.Regexp, rewriteTarget string, writer pagewriter.Writer, next http.Handler) http.Handler {
	return http.HandlerFunc(func(rw http.ResponseWriter, req *http.Request) {
		reqURL, err := url.ParseRequestURI(req.RequestURI)
		if err != nil {
			logger.Errorf("could not parse request URI: %v", err)
			writer.WriteErrorPage(rw, pagewriter.ErrorPageOpts{
				Status:    http.StatusInternalServerError,
				RequestID: middleware.GetRequestScope(req).RequestID,
				AppError:  fmt.Sprintf("Could not parse request URI: %v", err),
			})
			return
		}

		// Use the regex to rewrite the request path before proxying to the upstream.
		newURI := rewriteRegExp.ReplaceAllString(reqURL.Path, rewriteTarget)
		reqURL.Path, reqURL.RawQuery, err = splitPathAndQuery(reqURL.Query(), newURI)
		if err != nil {
			logger.Errorf("could not parse rewrite URI: %v", err)
			writer.WriteErrorPage(rw, pagewriter.ErrorPageOpts{
				Status:    http.StatusInternalServerError,
				RequestID: middleware.GetRequestScope(req).RequestID,
				AppError:  fmt.Sprintf("Could not parse rewrite URI: %v", err),
			})
			return
		}

		req.RequestURI = reqURL.String()
		next.ServeHTTP(rw, req)
	})
}

// splitPathAndQuery splits the rewritten path into the URL Path and the URL
// raw query. Any rewritten query values are appended to the original query
// values.
// This relies on the underlying URL library to encode the query string.
// For duplicate values it appends each as a separate value, e.g. ?foo=bar&foo=baz.
func splitPathAndQuery(originalQuery url.Values, raw string) (string, string, error) {
	s := strings.SplitN(raw, "?", 2)
	if len(s) == 1 {
		return s[0], originalQuery.Encode(), nil
	}

	queryValues, err := url.ParseQuery(s[1])
	if err != nil {
		return "", "", nil
	}

	for key, values := range queryValues {
		for _, value := range values {
			originalQuery.Add(key, value)
		}
	}

	return s[0], originalQuery.Encode(), nil
}

package upstream

import (
	"fmt"
	"net/http"
	"net/url"
	"regexp"
	"strings"

	"github.com/justinas/alice"
	"github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/apis/middleware"
	"github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/app/pagewriter"
	"github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/logger"
)

// newRewritePath creates a new middleware that will rewrite the request URI
// path before handing the request to the next server.
func newRewritePath(rewriteRegExp *regexp.Regexp, rewriteTarget string, writer pagewriter.Writer) alice.Constructor {
	return func(next http.Handler) http.Handler {
		return rewritePath(rewriteRegExp, rewriteTarget, writer, next)
	}
}

// rewritePath uses the regexp to rewrite the request URI based on the provided
// rewriteTarget.
func rewritePath(rewriteRegExp *regexp.Regexp, rewriteTarget string, writer pagewriter.Writer, next http.Handler) http.Handler {
	return http.HandlerFunc(func(rw http.ResponseWriter, req *http.Request) {
		reqURL, err := url.ParseRequestURI(req.RequestURI)
		if err != nil {
			logger.Errorf("could not parse request URI: %v", err)
			writer.WriteErrorPage(rw, pagewriter.ErrorPageOpts{
				Status:    http.StatusInternalServerError,
				RequestID: middleware.GetRequestScope(req).RequestID,
				AppError:  fmt.Sprintf("Could not parse request URI: %v", err),
			})
			return
		}

		// Use the regex to rewrite the request path before proxying to the upstream.
		newURI := rewriteRegExp.ReplaceAllString(reqURL.Path, rewriteTarget)
		reqURL.Path, reqURL.RawQuery, err = splitPathAndQuery(reqURL.Query(), newURI)
		if err != nil {
			logger.Errorf("could not parse rewrite URI: %v", err)
			writer.WriteErrorPage(rw, pagewriter.ErrorPageOpts{
				Status:    http.StatusInternalServerError,
				RequestID: middleware.GetRequestScope(req).RequestID,
				AppError:  fmt.Sprintf("Could not parse rewrite URI: %v", err),
			})
			return
		}

		req.RequestURI = reqURL.String()
		req.URL.Path = reqURL.Path // set path for websocket connections
		next.ServeHTTP(rw, req)
	})
}

// splitPathAndQuery splits the rewritten path into the URL Path and the URL
// raw query. Any rewritten query values are appended to the original query
// values.

🎬 ACTION
cat > /testbed/test_bug_reproduction.go << 'EOF'
package main

import (
	"crypto"
	"encoding/json"
	"fmt"
	"net/http"
	"net/http/httptest"

	middlewareapi "github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/apis/middleware"
	"github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/apis/options"
	"github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/app/pagewriter"
	"github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/upstream"
)

type TestResponse struct {
	Path string `json:"path"`
}

func main() {
	// Create a test HTTP server that echoes back the request path
	testServer := httptest.NewServer(http.HandlerFunc(func(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {
		response := TestResponse{Path: r.URL.Path}
		w.Header().Set("Content-Type", "application/json")
		json.NewEncoder(w).Encode(response)
	}))
	defer testServer.Close()

	// Create upstream configuration like in the bug report
	upstreamConfig := options.UpstreamConfig{
		Upstreams: []options.Upstream{
			{
				ID:            "app",
				Path:          "^/(.*)$",
				RewriteTarget: "/$1",
				URI:           testServer.URL,
			},
		},
	}

	sigData := &options.SignatureData{
		Hash: crypto.SHA256,
		Key:  "secret",
	}
	writer := &pagewriter.WriterFuncs{}

	proxy, err := upstream.NewProxy(upstreamConfig, sigData, writer)
	if err != nil {
		fmt.Printf("Error creating proxy: %v\n", err)
		return
	}

	// Test various paths
	testPaths := []string{
		"/",
		"/spec.js",
		"/api/test",
		"/foo/bar",
	}

	fmt.Println("Testing regex upstream rewrite:")
	for _, path := range testPaths {
		req := httptest.NewRequest("GET", "http://localhost"+path, nil)
		req = middlewareapi.AddRequestScope(req, &middlewareapi.RequestScope{})
		rw := httptest.NewRecorder()
		
		proxy.ServeHTTP(rw, req)
		
		var response TestResponse
		if err := json.Unmarshal(rw.Body.Bytes(), &response); err != nil {
			fmt.Printf("Request: %s => Status: %d, Error parsing response: %v\n", path, rw.Code, err)
		} else {
			fmt.Printf("Request: %s => Status: %d, Backend received: %s\n", path, rw.Code, response.Path)
			// Check if the path was correctly rewritten
			if response.Path != path {
				fmt.Printf("  ❌ FAIL: Expected path %s but got %s\n", path, response.Path)
			} else {
				fmt.Printf("  ✓ PASS\n")
			}
		}
	}
}
EOF

+package main
+
+import (
+"crypto"
+"encoding/json"
+"fmt"
+"net/http"
+"net/http/httptest"
+
+middlewareapi "github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/apis/middleware"
+"github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/apis/options"
+"github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/app/pagewriter"
+"github.com/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy/v7/pkg/upstream"
+)
+
+type TestResponse struct {
+Path string `json:"path"`
+}
+
+func main() {
+// Create a test HTTP server that echoes back the request path
+testServer := httptest.NewServer(http.HandlerFunc(func(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {
+response := TestResponse{Path: r.URL.Path}
+w.Header().Set("Content-Type", "application/json")
+json.NewEncoder(w).Encode(response)
+}))
+defer testServer.Close()
+
+// Create upstream configuration like in the bug report
+upstreamConfig := options.UpstreamConfig{
+Upstreams: []options.Upstream{
+{
+ID:            "app",
+Path:          "^/(.*)$",
+RewriteTarget: "/$1",
+URI:           testServer.URL,
+},
+},
+}
+
+sigData := &options.SignatureData{
+Hash: crypto.SHA256,
+Key:  "secret",
+}
+writer := &pagewriter.WriterFuncs{}
+
+proxy, err := upstream.NewProxy(upstreamConfig, sigData, writer)
+if err != nil {
+fmt.Printf("Error creating proxy: %v\n", err)
+return
+}
+
+// Test various paths
+testPaths := []string{
+"/",
+"/spec.js",
+"/api/test",
+"/foo/bar",
+}
+
+fmt.Println("Testing regex upstream rewrite:")
+for _, path := range testPaths {
+req := httptest.NewRequest("GET", "http://localhost"+path, nil)
+req = middlewareapi.AddRequestScope(req, &middlewareapi.RequestScope{})
+rw := httptest.NewRecorder()
+
+proxy.ServeHTTP(rw, req)
+
+var response TestResponse
+if err := json.Unmarshal(rw.Body.Bytes(), &response); err != nil {
+fmt.Printf("Request: %s => Status: %d, Error parsing response: %v\n", path, rw.Code, err)
+} else {
+fmt.Printf("Request: %s => Status: %d, Backend received: %s\n", path, rw.Code, response.Path)
+// Check if the path was correctly rewritten
+if response.Path != path {
+fmt.Printf("  ❌ FAIL: Expected path %s but got %s\n", path, response.Path)
+} else {
+fmt.Printf("  ✓ PASS\n")
+}
+}
+}
+}

+package main
+
+import (
+"fmt"
+"regexp"
+)
+
+func main() {
+// Test the regex from the bug report
+rewriteRegExp := regexp.MustCompile("^/(.*)$")
+rewriteTarget := "/$1"
+
+testPaths := []string{
+"/",
+"/spec.js",
+"/api/test",
+"/foo/bar",
+}
+
+for _, path := range testPaths {
+newURI := rewriteRegExp.ReplaceAllString(path, rewriteTarget)
+fmt.Printf("Path: %s => Rewritten: %s\n", path, newURI)
+}
+}
